**Summary.** This paper provides a complete analytical description of how a helical landscape affects the transport and dissipation of a Brownian particle. It demonstrates that the geometry of the landscape creates a direct link between axial and angular motion, which can be detected through cross-mobility and asymmetric energy absorption.

**Why it may be interesting.** The derivation of transport coefficients and dissipation in a non-stationary, non-equilibrium setting with broken symmetry is highly relevant to researchers studying open quantum systems and driven-dissipative dynamics.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how the helical geometry and damping anisotropy of a landscape influence the Brownian dynamics, mobility, and energy dissipation of an inertial particle.

**Main result.** The authors derive analytical expressions for the mobility tensor and show that chirality induces cross-response between axial and angular motion, as well as an asymmetry in energy dissipation.

**Method.** The study employs Langevin dynamics, linear response theory, and a projection operator approach to separate the dynamics into a stable subspace and a diffusive zero-mode.

**Model / system.** A classical Brownian particle with inertia moving in a 2D helical potential on a cylindrical surface, modeled using a harmonic well approximation and Langevin equations.

**Key observables.** Dynamical mobility tensor (diagonal and off-diagonal elements), momentum time-correlation functions, and energy dissipation rate.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Helix handedness (chirality), damping anisotropy, radius-to-pitch ratio, and temperature.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The potential is approximated as a harmonic well, the particle is structureless, and the system is treated within the framework of Markovian Langevin dynamics.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the helical potential landscape; Figure 4 shows momentum correlations; Figure 5 presents Nyquist plots of AC mobility; Figure 6 shows parametric variation of DC mobilities; Figure 7 shows energy dissipation absorption spectra.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the helical model, develops the stochastic framework using coordinate transformations, analyzes the isotropic and anisotropic damping regimes, derives the mobility tensor via linear response theory, and concludes with energy dissipation analysis.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study the Brownian dynamics and linear response of a particle with inertia moving in a 2-dimensional helical landscape imprinted on a cylindrical surface. In the harmonic well approximation, the deterministic motion separates into free propagation along the screw direction and harmonic motion in the transverse screw-normal direction. We show that for isotropic damping this simplification survives in the Langevin description, whereas anisotropic damping along the axial and angular directions couples the stochastic dynamics and destroys separability. The resulting anisotropic model is formulated as a linear Ornstein-Uhlenbeck process in phase space with a zero mode associated with diffusion along the screw coordinate, so that in an infinite system the full phase-space dynamics does not relax to a stationary distribution. To treat transport in this setting, we construct the stationary dynamics in the stable subspace obtained after projecting out the zero mode. This leads to a linear response theory for this system and yields closed analytical expressions for stationary time-correlation functions and the dynamical mobility tensor in both the time and frequency domains. The off-diagonal elements of the mobility tensor describe cross-response between axial forcing and angular motion, and between applied torque and axial transport. Consistent with time reversal symmetry, these cross mobilities are equal and provide a direct dynamical signature of the helical geometry. In addition, a simultaneous application of driving in both the axial and angular direction reveals asymmetry in energy dissipation rate due the helical landscape.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.23830"></a>
### [IntegrateUnitary.jl: A Julia package for symbolic integration over Haar measures](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23830v1)

**Authors:** Łukasz Pawela, Zbigniew Puchała  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23830v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `measurement-induced transitions` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.23830_figures/2605.23830_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 1. Architecture of IntegrateUnitary.jl. Scalar expressions follow the left path through normalization, substitution, expansion, and dispatch into the library lookup. Trace expressions are first analyzed by the symbolic trace logic, which reconstructs the Weingarten graph before entering the same dispatch stage. Common patterns are returned directly by the library lookup in O(1) time, while misses fall through to the specialized engines. Performance-critical internals (representation-theoretic quantities and Weingarten-related data) are memoized/cached for reuse.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** The authors present IntegrateUnitary.jl, a new Julia package designed for the symbolic integration of random matrix ensembles. It automates the complex Weingarten calculus and Wick contractions needed for quantum information theory, offering a scalable and high-performance alternative to existing Python and Mathematica tools.

**Why it may be interesting.** This tool automates the complex combinatorial task of calculating averages over random unitaries, which is essential for studying quantum chaos, scrambling, and entanglement in many-body dynamics and random quantum circuits.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The need for an efficient, automated, and symbolic tool to perform integration over the Haar measure of various compact groups and random matrix ensembles, which is computationally difficult due to the combinatorial complexity of Weingarten calculus.

**Main result.** The development of IntegrateUnitary.jl, a Julia package that provides a unified, high-performance implementation for symbolic integration over $U(d)$, $O(d)$, $Sp(d)$, and other ensembles, achieving significant speedups over existing tools like Haarpy and RTNI.

**Method.** The package utilizes the Symbolics.jl ecosystem, implementing Weingarten calculus, Wick contractions, the Murnaghan-Nakayama rule, and symplectic-orthogonal duality, alongside a coordinate-free symbolic trace interface.

**Model / system.** The software targets random matrix ensembles including Unitary, Orthogonal, and Symplectic groups, Ginibre ensembles, Circular ensembles (CUE, COE, CSE), permutation groups, and unitary $t$-designs.

**Key observables.** Polynomial moments of matrix entries, trace-polynomial integrals, purity, entanglement entropy, and quantum information metrics.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Dimension $d$ (treated as a symbolic variable), polynomial degree $k$, and the large-$d$ asymptotic limit.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Exact symbolic integration is limited to polynomial degrees $2k \lesssim 12$; certain workflows require concrete integer dimensions; $SU(d)$ support is currently limited to balanced polynomials.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates the software architecture and data flow for scalar and trace expressions; various tables compare performance benchmarks and scaling against other software packages.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the computational problem, describes the software architecture and core mathematical engines (Weingarten, Wick, etc.), presents performance benchmarks against existing tools, and demonstrates applications in quantum information tasks.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Symbolic integration over the Haar measure of compact groups is a computational cornerstone in quantum information science and random matrix theory. We present \texttt{IntegrateUnitary.jl}, a comprehensive Julia package for computing exact expectations of polynomial functions over a wide range of compact groups ($U(d)$, $O(d)$, $Sp(d)$, and $SU(d)$ for balanced polynomials), circular and Gaussian ensembles, Ginibre ensembles, permutation groups, random pure states, and unitary $t$-designs. The package provides a fully open-source implementation of the Weingarten calculus and Wick contractions with broad symbolic-$d$ support for entry-wise and trace-polynomial integrals, while selected workflows currently require concrete integer dimensions (including higher pure trace moments $|\mathrm{tr}(U)|^{2k}$ for $k > 1$ and HCIZ with \texttt{SymbolicMatrix} inputs, and direct matrix-valued integration of \texttt{SymbolicMatrix}/\texttt{SymbolicMatrixProduct} expressions), automatic asymptotic expansions, a high-level symbolic trace interface that reconstructs Weingarten graphs from index-free expressions, and a bridge to \texttt{ITensors.jl} for tensor network averaging. We discuss the underlying algorithms, including the Murnaghan-Nakayama rule and symplectic-orthogonal duality, and demonstrate that the package efficiently handles high-degree moments and quantum information metrics.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.23300"></a>
### [Local-Observable-Guided Generative Quantum Circuits for Degenerate Ground Spaces](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23300v1)

**Authors:** Yiying Chen, Lingxia Zhang, Yanzheng Zhu, Kaiyan Yang, Xiao Zeng, Zizhu Wang  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** numerical methods · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23300v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **2/5** · `exotic spin models in light-matter` **2/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.23300_figures/2605.23300_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1: Generative quantum circuit architecture. The network consists of a classical generative model followed by a parametrized quantum circuit (PQC). The encoder Eω maps an input θ0 ∼P(θ0) to a low-dimensional latent distribution z ∼N(µ,σ2). The decoder Dϕ then converts z into circuit parameters θ ∼Pω,ϕ(θ), which configure a PQC with depth L. Measurements are then performed to obtain an energy-diversity objective, and the parameters (ω,ϕ) are updated iteratively.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23300_figures/2605.23300_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2: Training dynamics for the MG model. Shown are the batch-mean energy (red), the batch-mean pairwise fidelity (blue), and the sum of cosine similarities l(1) + l(2)</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.23300_figures/2605.23300_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 3: Overlap distributions of accepted states {|ψi〉}1500 i=1 with the MG ground-state basis {|gi〉}k i=1. The plots combine probability densities (the half-violin plot on the left) with quartile statistics (the box-and-whisker plot on the right box). The broad distributions indicate a diverse generated ensemble covering the full degenerate ground space.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.23300_figures/2605.23300_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 4: Training dynamics for the symmetry-encoded AKLT model at system size N = 10. Shown are the batch-mean energy (red), the batch-mean pairwise fidelity (blue), and the sum of cosine similarities l(1) + l(2) edge (green). The inset highlights the first 200 iterations. The dynamics exhibit an initial diversity-dominated spreading stage followed by an energy-dominated concentration into the degenerate ground space. Finally, the energy converges to the ground-state energy with low batch-mean pairwise fidelity.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.23300_figures/2605.23300_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 5: Overlap distributions of accepted states {|ψi〉}1500 i=1 with the symmetry-encoded AKLT ground-state basis {|gi〉}4 i=1 at system size N = 10. The half-violin plot represents the probability density, and the box-and-whisker plot summarizes the quartiles and spread. The broad distributions indicate that all basis directions are represented across the generated ensemble.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** The paper introduces a generative quantum circuit framework designed to learn the entire degenerate ground-state space of many-body Hamiltonians. By optimizing an energy-diversity objective using local observables, the method avoids mode collapse and accurately captures the geometric structure of the ground-state manifold. It demonstrates high robustness to sampling noise and successful application to various spin-chain models.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides a scalable way to explore degenerate manifolds and topological ground spaces using local measurements, which is highly relevant for characterizing many-body phases in both simulated and near-term quantum hardware.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Recovering the full degenerate ground-state manifold of quantum many-body systems, which is challenging because existing methods often capture individual states but fail to represent the entire degenerate space without mode collapse.

**Main result.** The proposed hybrid generative quantum circuit successfully reproduces the full span and internal feature-space geometry of degenerate ground spaces in the Majumdar-Ghosh, AKLT, and spin-1 XXZ models, even under finite-shot noise.

**Method.** A hybrid framework combining a classical generative model (VGON) with a parameterized quantum circuit (PQC), using an energy-diversity loss function based on local observable correlators to prevent representation collapse.

**Model / system.** The study benchmarks on several 1D spin models: the spin-1/2 Majumdar-Ghosh model, the spin-1 AKLT model (with symmetry-encoded qutrit mapping), and the spin-1 XXZ chain at the first-order phase transition point.

**Key observables.** Local one-body magnetizations, nearest-neighbor two-body Pauli correlations, effective rank of the state matrix, ground-space overlap score, and principal angles.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Energy-diversity weight (lambda_2) annealing schedule, shot-adaptive training budget, and relative error tolerance (epsilon) for rank determination.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Benchmark certification is limited to system sizes accessible by Exact Diagonalization; numerical rank determination assumes a fixed relative error tolerance.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the generative architecture; Figure 2 illustrates training dynamics (energy vs. fidelity); Figures 8-9 show circuit ansatze for spin-1/2 and spin-1; Figures 10-15 present overlap decompositions and cosine-similarity heatmaps comparing exact vs. generated states.

**Paper structure.** Introduction to the degeneracy problem, description of the hybrid generative architecture and energy-diversity objective, detailed implementation of circuit ansatze for different spin models, benchmarking results on MG, AKLT, and XXZ models, and analysis of robustness under finite-shot noise.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Searching for degenerate ground spaces in quantum many-body systems is central to understanding spontaneous symmetry breaking and topological order. Although existing numerical methods can approximate individual ground states with high accuracy, recovering the full degenerate space remains a substantial challenge. Here we tackle this problem using a hybrid generative quantum circuit that combines a classical generative model with an expressive parameterized quantum circuit (PQC). The classical model learns a distribution over PQC parameters, enabling the sampling of an ensemble of ground states, while the PQC ensures compatibility with quantum hardware. To promote both low energy and state diversity, we define an energy-diversity objective composed of an energy-minimization term and cosine-similarity penalties derived from local observable correlators. These local descriptors provide a scalable, measurement-efficient means of distinguishing distinct ground states. We benchmark the framework on the Majumdar-Ghosh model, the Affleck-Kennedy-Lieb-Tasaki model, and the spin-1 XXZ chain, which realize distinct mechanisms of degeneracy. In all cases, the method produces a diverse ensemble whose linear span accurately reproduces the target ground space, in some instances, it identifies an approximately orthogonal basis within the learned ensemble. We further show that the framework remains robust under shot-based estimation and can still recover the degenerate ground space with a reduced measurement budget.

</details>

### [Non-Hermitian Landau Levels](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23613v1)

**Summary.** This paper develops the theory of Landau levels in the presence of a complex-valued magnetic field. It demonstrates that such fields lead to complex energy spectra and spiral-shaped particle trajectories. The findings suggest new ways to implement non-Hermitian physics in platforms like topoelectrical circuits and ultracold atoms.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant for researchers in open quantum systems and many-body dynamics as it provides a fundamental framework for understanding how non-Hermiticity (via complex magnetic fields) alters topological features and transport properties like the Lorentz force.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the properties, topology, and dynamics of Landau levels in two-dimensional systems subject to a complex-valued perpendicular magnetic field.

**Main result.** The authors derive complex-valued, highly degenerate energy spectra and show that the imaginary part of the magnetic field induces a drag force, turning circular cyclotron motion into spiral trajectories.

**Method.** The study uses an algebraic approach with creation and annihilation operators, a biorthogonal formalism for non-Hermitian eigenstates, and numerical simulations of a non-Hermitian Harper-Hofstadter lattice model.

**Model / system.** A 2D system of charged particles in a complex magnetic field, modeled both in the continuum using a non-Hermitian Hamiltonian and on a square lattice via a non-Hermitian Harper-Hofstadter model.

**Key observables.** Complex eigenenergies, biorthogonal eigenstates, wave packet center-of-mass trajectories, and effective mass.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Complex magnetic field B = Re(B) + iIm(B), cyclotron frequency, magnetic length, and wave packet width.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes a semiclassical framework for wave packet dynamics and requires Re(B) > |Im(B)| for wavefunction square-integrability in the Landau gauge.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows complex eigenenergies and numerical right eigenstates; Figure 2 displays wave packet trajectories (spiraling motion); Figure 3 shows effective mass as a function of wave packet width.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins with the formulation of the continuum theory and algebraic derivation of complex Landau levels, moves to the analysis of gauge dependence and localization, then transitions to lattice model simulations and semiclassical wave packet dynamics, and concludes with an investigation of effective mass dependence.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We formulate non-Hermitian Landau levels in two-dimensional systems under a complex perpendicular magnetic field. In the symmetric gauge, we derive their discretely spaced, highly degenerate complex spectra and biorthogonal eigenstates, and clarify the role of non-unitary gauge transformations. A non-Hermitian Harper-Hofstadter lattice model confirms the continuum theory and reveals Gaussian wave packet dynamics governed by semiclassical equations with a complex Lorentz force, pointing to possible experimental realizations of complex magnetic fields.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.23734"></a>
### [The Floquet-Magnus expansion of unbounded operators](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23734v1)

**Authors:** Daniel Burgarth, Robin Hillier, Davide Lonigro, Leonhard Richter  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23734v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `Tavis-Cummings & cavity-many-emitter` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5** · `scars & prethermalization` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.23734_figures/2605.23734_page2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 2</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23734_figures/2605.23734_page3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 3</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.23734_figures/2605.23734_page4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 4</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.23734_figures/2605.23734_page5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 5</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.23734_figures/2605.23734_page6.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 6</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper extends the Floquet-Magnus expansion from bounded to unbounded operators, allowing for a rigorous treatment of periodically driven quantum systems. It introduces a new construction that provides explicit error bounds in the high-frequency limit even when the expansion series itself does not converge. The method is successfully demonstrated on the quantum Rabi model and the driven harmonic oscillator.

**Why it may be interesting.** This provides a rigorous mathematical foundation for using effective Hamiltonians in quantum optics and many-body physics, where unbounded operators (like position/momentum or photon number) are standard, and offers improved error scaling in the high-frequency regime.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The standard Floquet-Magnus expansion is mathematically restricted to bounded Hamiltonians, making it difficult to rigorously treat physically relevant unbounded operators in periodically driven systems.

**Main result.** The authors develop a nonperturbative framework that extends the Floquet-Magnus expansion to a broad class of unbounded Hamiltonians, providing explicit error bounds that vanish in the high-frequency limit without requiring the convergence of the expansion series.

**Method.** An iterative integration-by-parts technique and a constructive framework based on Kato's theory of evolution equations are used to derive effective Hamiltonians and error estimates.

**Model / system.** The framework is applied to the quantum Rabi Hamiltonian in the interaction picture and a periodically driven quantum harmonic oscillator.

**Key observables.** Unitary propagators and the difference between exact and approximated dynamics.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The driving period (T), the high-frequency limit (T approaching 0), and the energy scale defined by a reference self-adjoint operator (H0).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The Hamiltonians must satisfy specific regularity and stability properties (Properties A.1-A.9 and C.1-C.7), including relative boundedness and well-defined commutator structures.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of unbounded operators, presents a nonperturbative integration-by-parts framework, establishes theorems for error control and propagator difference, proves the construction reproduces the Floquet-Magnus expansion, and demonstrates the method via the quantum Rabi and driven harmonic oscillator models.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

The Floquet-Magnus expansion is a widely used tool to derive effective descriptions of time-periodic quantum systems by approximating their dynamics with a time-independent Hamiltonian. However, its standard formulation is, strictly speaking, restricted to bounded Hamiltonians. In this work, we extend its definition and analysis to a broad class of time-periodic unbounded Hamiltonians. Our approach is based on an a priori distinct nonperturbative framework for the construction of effective Hamiltonians, which we show to reproduce the Floquet-Magnus expansion. A particular strength of our framework is that it allows us to prove that the resulting effective dynamics approximates the original time evolution propagators to arbitrary order in the high-frequency limit without requiring convergence of the Floquet-Magnus expansion, a condition that is already highly restrictive even in the bounded setting. We illustrate the scope of the method on representative models: the quantum Rabi Hamiltonian in the interaction picture, and the periodically driven quantum harmonic oscillator.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.23455"></a>
### [Sequential Spatiotemporal Magnetic-Field Reconstruction via Quantum Hamiltonian Learning with NV-Center Spin-1 Hamiltonians](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23455v1)

**Authors:** Hiroshi Yamauchi, Sophie Colleen Stearn, Samuel Tovey  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23455v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `quantum measurements` **3/5** · `spintronics-quantum-optics interface` **3/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.23455_figures/2605.23455_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1. Recovery of spatial magnetic-field structure. (a) Initial prior map at t = 0, generated from a random Bernoulli initialization, showing no coherent global organization. (b) Reconstructed field at the final analyzed frame t = 15, ob- tained through sequential inference under the NV Hamilto- nian model, with RMSE = 7.037 × 10−7 T. The emergence of the maze-like structure demonstrates that the reconstruction is achieved through inference rather than direct observation.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23455_figures/2605.23455_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 3. Representative k-step convergence behavior for three windows. Top row: expected information gain (EIG) as a function of k. Bottom row: corresponding empirical measure- ment probabilities ¯p. The EIG decreases across steps, while ¯p stabilizes after the early updates, consistent with local pos- terior concentration.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.23455_figures/2605.23455_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2. Adaptive measurement behavior. (a) Distribution of empirical measurement probabilities ˆp at the initial step (k = 0) and after adaptive updates (k = 11). (b) Expected information gain (EIG) as a function of the adaptive step k, showing rapid decay and saturation.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.23455_figures/2605.23455_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 3 shows the detailed convergence behavior for three representative windows. While all windows exhibit a general decrease in ex- pected information gain, the initial magnitude and de- cay rate differ across spatial locations. This indicates that the local identifiability of the field depends on the underlying field configuration within each window. In particular, windows with stronger local gradients ex- hibit higher initial EIG and faster convergence, whereas more homogeneous regions show lower initial information gain and slower convergence. This heterogeneity demonstrates that the adaptive in- ference mechanism naturally allocates measurement ef- fort according to local information...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.23455_figures/2605.23455_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 5. Reconstruction error and scan strategy comparison. (a) RMSE and MAE over frames for H+V scan. (b) Compar- ison of RMSE and MAE for H-only, V-only, and H+V scans at the final frame.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper proposes a method to reconstruct time-varying 2D magnetic fields by combining local quantum Hamiltonian learning with sequential Bayesian updates. Using NV-center spin-1 dynamics as a model, the authors demonstrate that while spatial structures can be recovered accurately, estimating global interaction parameters remains challenging due to parameter degeneracy and bias.

**Why it may be interesting.** It integrates Quantum Hamiltonian Learning with spatiotemporal Bayesian filtering, addressing the complex task of reconstructing global many-body parameters (J) and local fields simultaneously in a dynamic setting.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The sequential spatiotemporal reconstruction of a dynamic, 2D magnetic field from local, noisy, and overlapping observations using quantum sensors.

**Main result.** The framework successfully recovers large-scale spatial structures (maze-like patterns) with low RMSE, though the global coupling parameter J remains partially identifiable and biased.

**Method.** A sequential Bayesian inference framework using a particle-based Monte Carlo estimator and an adaptive control policy based on expected information gain and leakage-aware scoring.

**Model / system.** A nitrogen-vacancy (NV) center spin-1 system in diamond, modeled via a rotating-frame Hamiltonian that includes local magnetic field detuning, transverse strain, and long-range dipolar interactions.

**Key observables.** Ramsey-type readout operators, Classical Fisher Information (CFI), Quantum Fisher Information (QFI), and spin-1 leakage to the |-1> state.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Local magnetic field magnitudes (Bt), shared dipolar coupling parameter (J), and interrogation time (T).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The study uses a numerical 'trusted-simulator' (exact diagonalization) rather than hardware-in-the-loop; it assumes an idealized binomial shot model for measurements.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the transition from random prior to reconstructed field; Figure 2 shows decay of expected information gain; Figure 3 shows local convergence; Figure 4 tracks coupling J estimation; Figure 6 shows the impact of scan geometry (H vs V vs H+V).

**Paper structure.** The paper defines the spatiotemporal reconstruction problem, introduces the NV spin-1 Hamiltonian model, details the sequential Bayesian/SMC framework and adaptive control policy, presents numerical results on field reconstruction and coupling estimation, and discusses metrological trade-offs and limitations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We propose a quantum-Hamiltonian-learning-based sequential reconstruction framework for dynamic two-dimensional magnetic fields using a local likelihood model derived from a nitrogen-vacancy center spin-1 Hamiltonian. The latent field is not observed directly; instead, local measurements are generated through nitrogen-vacancy spin dynamics governed by local magnetic-field values and a shared dipolar coupling parameter. Sequential Bayesian updates over overlapping scan windows are combined with temporal posterior propagation to reconstruct the evolving field.   Numerical experiments on synthetic maze-like magnetic-field sequences show that the proposed method recovers the dominant spatial structure, achieving a root-mean-square error of \(7.037\times10^{-7}\,\mathrm{T}\) at the final frame. Adaptive diagnostics show decreasing expected information gain and stable local convergence. Fisher-information and leakage diagnostics reveal a sensitivity--leakage tradeoff under long-interrogation controls, and the implemented adaptive policy incorporates leakage-aware control scoring while leaving the likelihood itself unchanged. Combined horizontal and vertical scans improve reconstruction relative to single-direction acquisition. The shared coupling parameter \(J\) is only partially identifiable: its posterior becomes narrow but remains frame-dependent and biased.   At the final checkpoint, the coupling posterior reaches \(J_{\rm std}=87.0\,\mathrm{Hz}\), close to a finite-time product-state reference benchmark of \(73.3\,\mathrm{Hz}\), while remaining \(3.35\times\) above a gain-extrapolated ideal-state benchmark. The posterior mean, however, remains biased by \(326.9\,\mathrm{Hz}\), indicating that posterior concentration alone does not imply unbiased coupling identifiability.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.23625"></a>
### [Atom-Photon Bound States in Fractal Photonic Lattices: Localization Length and Anomalous Diffusion](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23625v1)

**Authors:** Florian Bönsel, Flore K. Kunst, Federico Roccati  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23625v1>

(c) In the regular case, a quadratic band edge ω(k) −ωedge ∼|k|2 yields the familiar scaling ξ ∼∆−1/2 for the localization length ξ of the atom-photon bound state, with ∆as the emitter detuning from the lower band edge. (d) In a fractal bath, translational invariance and ordinary bands are absent; instead the low-energy scaling is set by the walk dimension through E ∼L−dw, leading to the generalized law ξ ∼∆−1/dw, with the walk dimension dw (defined in the text). For a regular two-dimensional lattice, dw = 2 (and coincides with the spatial dimension), whereas for the Sierpi´nski...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23625_figures/2605.23625_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 2. Representative self-similar photonic graphs. Nested fractals, such as Sierpi´nski gaskets, can be disconnected by removing finitely many ver- tices at each scale, here three sites for the b = 2 gasket [blue crosses for g = 2 in (a)], whereas Sierpi´nski carpets remain connected across arbitrarily many channels.</sub>

</details>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.23625_figures/2605.23625_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 4. Far-field localization length. The rescaled localiza- tion length ξ · ∆1/2 is shown as a function of detuning ∆. A horizontal line corresponds to the regular-lattice bench- mark ξ ∼∆−1/2, while systematic power-law drifts reveal the fractal exponent 1/dw. Data are extracted along the outer boundary of each fractal, where d(x, x0) coincides with the Euclidean arc length. The following generations are taken for the fractals: Gasket (b = 2): g = 7, Gasket (b = 3): g = 5, Carpet (9, 1): g = 5, Carpet (16, 4): g = 4, Pyramid: g = 6, Vicsek: g = 5, Square: L = 151 × 151 sites.</sub>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.23625_figures/2605.23625_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 5. Near-field scaling of atom-photon bound states. The quantity δψ(r)/δψ(rmin) with δψ(r) = |ψ(x0) −ψ(x)|</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that the spatial extent of atom-photon bound states in fractal photonic lattices is governed by the fractal's walk dimension rather than standard effective mass. It provides a generalized scaling law for localization and shows how the near-field profile reflects the underlying fractal transport properties.

**Why it may be interesting.** It extends waveguide QED to non-translational invariant geometries and establishes a direct link between quantum bound-state profiles and classical anomalous diffusion exponents.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how the fractal geometry of a photonic bath reshapes the localization length and spatial profile of atom-photon bound states.

**Main result.** The far-field localization length scales as xi ~ Delta^(-1/dw), where dw is the walk dimension of the fractal, and the near-field amplitude follows an algebraic scaling related to fractal transport properties.

**Method.** Analytical derivation using the heat kernel and saddle-point approximation of the Green's function, complemented by numerical exact diagonalization on various fractal graphs.

**Model / system.** A two-level emitter coupled to a photonic bath arranged in self-similar fractal lattices (e.g., Sierpinski gaskets, carpets, and Vicsek graphs) described by a tight-binding Hamiltonian.

**Key observables.** Localization length (xi), detuning (Delta), near-field amplitude difference, and fractal dimensions (dw, ds, df).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Detuning from the spectral edge (Delta), walk dimension (dw), spectral dimension (ds), and the distinction between finitely ramified and infinitely ramified fractals.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The bath Hamiltonian is rendered Laplacian-like by compensating for connectivity inhomogeneities with on-site potentials; the study focuses on the regime near the lower spectral edge.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares regular vs. fractal lattices and their dispersion/diffusion; Figure 4 shows the rescaled localization length scaling with detuning; Figure 5 illustrates near-field amplitude scaling for different fractal types.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of atom-photon bound states in non-periodic media, develops an analytical framework using the heat kernel, provides numerical validation on various fractal geometries, and discusses the scaling of near-field and far-field regimes.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study atom-photon bound states seeded by two-level emitters coupled to self-similar photonic lattices. By expressing the photonic Green's function through the heat kernel, we show that the far-field localization length obeys $ξ\sim Δ^{-1/d_w}$, with the detuning $Δ$ from the lower spectral edge and the walk dimension $d_w$ of the underlying fractal. This scaling is controlled by anomalous diffusion and does not rely on translational invariance or a band-edge effective-mass approximation. Exact diagonalization on Sierpiński gaskets, pyramids, Vicsek graphs, and Sierpiński carpets confirms the far-field prediction once the bath Hamiltonian is rendered Laplacian-like by compensating the local inhomogeneity in the connectivities with on-site potentials. In the near field, the bound-state amplitude exhibits an additional algebraic variation. For nested finitely ramified fractals, the corresponding exponent agrees with the classical resistance/ first-passage scaling, whereas Sierpiński carpets display clear deviations from this simple law. Our results extend structured-bath waveguide QED to self-similar non-periodic geometries and connect bound-state profiles to transport exponents of the underlying fractal lattice.

</details>

### [Electron-Photon Spatial Entanglement in Coherent Cathodoluminescence](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23335v1)

**Summary.** This paper develops a theoretical framework to quantify spatial entanglement between electrons and photons in coherent cathodoluminescence. It classifies the system into wave-like, particle-like, and classical regimes based on beam coherence and photon bandwidth. The findings provide a roadmap for using electron microscopy as a platform for quantum-enabled imaging and sensing.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a bridge between electron microscopy and quantum optics by treating electron-photon scattering as a source of continuous-variable entanglement, relevant to quantum imaging and sensing.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Quantifying the degree and nature of electron-photon spatial entanglement in coherent cathodoluminescence (CL) and determining how it depends on electron-beam properties like transverse coherence.

**Main result.** The study identifies three distinct entanglement regimes (wave-like, particle-like, and classical) and reveals that strong spatial entanglement emerges when the electron's transverse coherence length is large and the photon spectral width is optimized.

**Method.** A theoretical framework that reconstructs the scattered electron-photon state from the luminescence spectrum and evaluates entanglement using subsystem purity and an EPR-type uncertainty criterion.

**Model / system.** A single-electron beam interacting with a radiation field (specifically transition radiation) in a weak-coupling regime, modeled using a Hamiltonian for free electrons and photons with an interaction term.

**Key observables.** Subsystem purity (P_sc), EPR-type uncertainty product (D^2_sc), and joint probability distributions for position and wavevector.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Electron transverse and longitudinal coherence lengths (L_el_perp, L_el_parallel), photon spectral width (Delta_lambda_ph), and electron transverse wavenumber width (Delta_q_el_perp).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is translationally invariant in the transverse plane, the interaction is in the weak-coupling regime, and the momentum change of the electron is much smaller than its incident momentum.

**Figures summary.** Fig 1 illustrates the CL process; Fig 2 maps the entanglement regimes (A, B, C) against beam parameters; Fig 5 shows longitudinal entanglement via purity; Fig 6 shows joint probability distributions; Fig 7 examines the impact of phase uncertainty on the EPR criterion.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by defining the interaction model and state reconstruction framework, proceeds to classify entanglement regimes using purity and EPR criteria, analyzes the influence of electron beam coherence, and concludes with an investigation into the impact of unknown phase factors.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Electron-photon quantum entanglement in an electron microscope paves the way for a new quantum platform, enabling the integration of quantum functionalities into electron microscopy and opening opportunities for quantum imaging and quantum sensing at the nanoscale. To realize such a platform, it is crucial to understand the degree and nature of electron-photon entanglement in cathodoluminescence (CL). However, its dependence on electron-beam properties, particularly transverse coherence, remains unclear. Here, we present a theoretical framework describing the quantum state of an electron-photon pair generated in coherent CL, specifically for transition radiation. By expressing the scattered state directly via the luminescence spectrum, we evaluate the entanglement using both subsystem purity and an Einstein-Podolsky-Rosen-type criterion. These two measures enable a clear distinction between wave-like, particle-like, and classical regimes in terms of spatial and momentum entanglement in the electron-photon system. Our analysis identifies the roles of the electron's transverse and longitudinal coherence, as well as the photon's spectral width, and reveals the conditions under which strong spatial entanglement emerges. This unified perspective clarifies the nature of electron-photon quantum correlations in coherent CL, leading to quantum-enabled functionalities in electron microscopy.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.23206"></a>
### [Yukawa-Screened Bose-Star Condensation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23206v1)

**Authors:** Jiajun Chen  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum gases · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23206v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

**Summary.** This paper explores how Yukawa-type screened interactions affect the formation of Bose-stars. It demonstrates that a finite interaction range delays the condensation process and results in less compact, broader density profiles. The findings are supported by both analytical kinetic theory and numerical simulations.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides insights into how modifying the range of interactions affects the relaxation dynamics and structural stability of many-body bosonic systems, which is highly relevant to the study of non-equilibrium dynamics in ultracold gases.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how finite-range Yukawa interactions modify the formation, internal structure, and condensation timescale of Bose-stars compared to the standard long-range Newtonian case.

**Main result.** Yukawa screening broadens the Bose-star density profile and systematically delays the condensation timescale by suppressing infrared kinetic relaxation.

**Method.** The study uses analytical derivation of a screened kinetic condensation formula and fully dynamical pseudospectral simulations with imaginary-time relaxation for ground-state profiles.

**Model / system.** A Yukawa-Schrödinger-Poisson (YSP) system representing a self-gravitating bosonic gas (such as axion dark matter) with a screened gravitational potential.

**Key observables.** Bose-star density profiles, condensation timescale, and projected density field snapshots.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Yukawa screening mass (mu_Y), boson mass (m), and the dimensionless screening parameter (e*mu_Y).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The Yukawa interaction is treated phenomenologically as a screened gravitational potential; the system is studied in a periodic box with homogeneous and isotropic initial conditions.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the broadening of static Bose-star profiles with increasing screening; Figure 2 displays density field snapshots demonstrating delayed formation; Figure 3 shows the evolution of density profiles; Figure 4 shows the evolution of maximum density; Figure 5 compares predicted vs. measured condensation times.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the YSP model, derives an analytical formula for screened kinetic condensation, presents static solutions for Bose-star profiles, details dynamical pseudospectral simulations, and concludes by validating the analytical predictions against numerical results.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study Bose-star formation in a Yukawa-Schrödinger-Poisson (YSP) system. A finite interaction range suppresses the infrared kinetic relaxation responsible for Bose-star condensation, modifying both the equilibrium Bose-star structure and the condensation timescale. We derive a screened kinetic condensation formula in which the ordinary gravitational Coulomb logarithm is replaced by a finite Yukawa transport logarithm. Static YSP solutions show that Yukawa screening broadens the Bose-star density profile relative to the ordinary Newtonian soliton. Fully dynamical pseudospectral simulations with homogeneous and isotropic initial conditions demonstrate that Yukawa screening systematically delays Bose-star condensation, in good agreement with the screened kinetic prediction after fitting a single overall normalization parameter.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.23214"></a>
### [Coverage Analysis of Rydberg Atom Quantum Receiver Arrays: A Stochastic Geometry Approach](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23214v1)

**Authors:** Dongnan Xia, Cunhua Pan, Hong Ren, Dongsheng Sui, Qihao Peng, Jiangzhou Wang  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23214v1>

<sub>Fig. 3(c) also plots the coverage as a function of λb, with λu = λb. For θ = 0 and 10 dB, the optimized RAQR attains higher coverage than the conventional receiver at low BS densities, while the advantage disappears as the network becomes denser. The two crossover points occur at λb ≈4.4×10−5 m−2 and λb ≈5.5×10−5 m−2, respectively. Beyond these points, the RAQR coverage falls steeply with λb, because Bussgang distortion scales as ¯σ6 in, i.e., cubically in λb, while the conventional noise grows only linearly. These crossovers indicate that the operating point should balance small-signal sensitivity with receiver linearity.</sub>

**Summary.** This paper analyzes the performance of Rydberg-based quantum receivers in wireless networks using stochastic geometry. It reveals a fundamental tradeoff where the advantage of low quantum noise is lost in dense networks due to nonlinear distortion from aggregate interference.

**Why it may be interesting.** It bridges microscopic open quantum system dynamics (Lindblad equation) with macroscopic network theory, exploring how nonlinearities in quantum transducers affect large-scale system reliability.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Determining whether the high sensitivity of Rydberg Atom Quantum Receivers (RAQRs) translates to improved network-level reliability in dense wireless deployments, specifically considering the impact of nonlinear distortion caused by aggregate interference.

**Main result.** RAQRs outperform conventional receivers in sparse, noise-limited networks, but in dense networks, nonlinear distortion (Bussgang distortion) can cause RAQR performance to fall below that of conventional receivers.

**Method.** The authors use a stochastic geometry approach with a Poisson Point Process, applying Bussgang decomposition to linearize the third-order nonlinear atomic response and deriving analytical expressions for coverage probability.

**Model / system.** A four-level ladder-type Rydberg atomic system (|1> to |4>) interacting with RF fields, modeled via the Lindblad master equation and a third-order complex baseband model including linear gain and cubic nonlinearity.

**Key observables.** SINR (Signal-to-Interference-plus-Noise Ratio), coverage probability, and effective noise.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Base station density (lambda_b), antenna array size (M_r), nonlinearity ratio (|c3/c1|), and path-loss exponent (alpha).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The input signal is assumed to be a circularly symmetric complex Gaussian process, and the network is modeled as a homogeneous Poisson Point Process.

**Figures summary.** Comparison of 133Cs and 85Rb performance; coverage probability vs. SINR threshold for various densities; impact of array scaling (M_r) and receiver correlation on coverage.

**Paper structure.** The paper moves from a microscopic atomic master equation to a macroscopic network-level coverage analysis, establishing a nonlinear baseband model, applying linearization techniques, and validating results via Monte Carlo simulations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Rydberg atomic quantum receivers (RAQRs) offer quantum-limited sensitivity and broadband tunability. It is not obvious whether this device-level advantage also improves network reliability, since in dense deployments, aggregate interference can push the atomic transducer out of its small-signal regime. This paper addresses the question by embedding the RAQR front end into a stochastic geometry (SG) coverage analysis. Starting with the atomic master equation and balanced coherent optical detection, we derive a third-order complex baseband model that retains both the linear gain and the leading cubic nonlinearity. A Bussgang decomposition converts the per-element nonlinear response into an equivalent linear gain plus a distance-dependent distortion noise. Using this equivalent model, we derive the post maximal-ratio combining (MRC) SINR and obtain tractable expressions for the conditional and spatially averaged coverage probabilities. The analytical results show that RAQRs outperform conventional receivers in sparse deployments. However, when the base station (BS) density becomes large, nonlinear distortion reduces this advantage and may make RAQRs perform worse. Simulation results validate the analytical expressions and confirm that the central design tradeoff is between linear gain and cubic nonlinearity.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.23286"></a>
### [Modeling the Quantum Photon Statistics in Hybrid Light-Matter Integrated Circuits](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23286v1)

**Authors:** Mathias Van Regemortel, Vincenzo Ardizzone, Eugenio Maggiolini, Armando Rastelli, Daniele Sanvitto, Thomas Van Vaerenbergh  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23286v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `interference shaping light` **3/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **3/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.23286_figures/2605.23286_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 1: The experimental LP dispersion in an AlGaAs waveguide with GaAs quantum wells and derived quantities. (a) Photoluminscence of the dispersion of the guided polaritonic mode extracted from an input/output diffraction grating; vertical axis shows the energy of the polariton mode while the horizontal axis is the wavevector along the propagation direction. (b) Group velocity vg (blue solid, left axis) and exciton fraction |uk|2 (red dashed, right axis) obtained from the dispersion in (a).</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23286_figures/2605.23286_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 2: The Mach-Zehnder interferometer setup for generating antibunched photon statistic. After the first 50 : 50 beam splitter (BS) coupler, one arm (the local oscillator) has a tunable phase shift ϕLO, while the other couples in the nonlinear waveguide. After the second coupler a HBT experiment is performed of the signal in the two arms, labeled with the mode index l = 0, 1.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.23286_figures/2605.23286_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 3: Results for the out-coupled photon statistics of a BS with coupling θout = 0.2π, when modulating the MZI LO phase within the range ϕLO ∈{0, 2π} for an incoming pulse of |α|2 = 1 and 1 mm waveguide coupling at u2 k = 0.3 exciton fraction. (a) The varying output intensity across the two modes, on log-scale. (b)-(d) Intensity correlations, intra-mode (blue–orange, solid), cross-correlations (black, dot-dashed) and the coherent correlation for reference (gray, dotted), at the reported nonlinearities. Sub-Poissonian statistics, reaching g(2) ll &lt; 0.5 at ℏg = 700 µeV µm2 is observed in the antisymmetric output arm around ϕLO/2π ≈0.45, just below ϕLO = π</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.23286_figures/2605.23286_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 4: The prototype architecture studied for the first experiments. It consists of L = 6 coupled waveguides, integrated in a 1 mm architecture consisting of D = 5 stacked layers of coupling gates. The signal is injected in waveguides l = 0 and l = 5 and the output signals of the waveguides are detected individually. It is assumed that all couplers are uniform across the circuit, but the circuit coupling J∆t and U∆t will rescale in function of the input wavevector k.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2605.23286_figures/2605.23286_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 5: The simulation results of a circuit of L = 6 waveguides and depth D = 5, for experimentally reported exciton interaction strengths, for zero losses and φrel = 0.6π. (a) The output pulse intensities (pulse photon number) for ℏg = 10µeV µm2 (indistinguishable from ℏg = [50, 700] µeV µm2). (b) The expected intra-pulse intensity-intensity correlations. Strong antibunched photon statistics is witnessed at low output intensities. In all cases, there is sharp crossover from antibunching to bunching statistics around the low-intensity values k ≈[0.15, 0.27] µm−1</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper presents a new theoretical framework for predicting non-classical photon statistics in hybrid (Al)GaAs polaritonic integrated circuits. It demonstrates how engineered features like slow-light dispersion and MZI configurations can amplify photon antibunching and bunching. The work provides a roadmap for achieving quantum-level light manipulation on-chip.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a bridge between semiconductor device physics and quantum optics, offering a scalable framework for designing integrated quantum photonic circuits using nonlinear light-matter interactions.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The lack of a quantitative theoretical framework to connect realistic waveguide parameters to measurable non-classical photon statistics in hybrid light-matter integrated circuits.

**Main result.** The development of a comprehensive framework (qPIC) that predicts quantum signatures like photon antibunching and demonstrates that slow-light engineering can amplify nonlinearities to achieve non-Gaussian statistics.

**Method.** Mapping pulsed nonlinear waveguide dynamics onto a bosonic quantum circuit representation using the Matrix Product State Density Operator (MPDO) framework and Kraus operators for dissipation.

**Model / system.** Hybrid (Al)GaAs light-matter integrated circuits supporting exciton-polaritons, modeled via a Kerr-type Hamiltonian in both single-waveguide MZI and multi-mode coupled-waveguide architectures.

**Key observables.** Photon-number output statistics, second-order correlation function g(2)(0) (antibunching and bunching), signal intensity, and intensity-intensity correlation matrices.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Rabi splitting, exciton interaction constant, group velocity (v_g), Hopfield coefficients, and local oscillator phase.

**Assumptions / limitations.** 1-D longitudinal wavevector approximation, pulse envelope invariance over time, and local Fock-space truncation.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows polariton dispersion and derived group velocity; Figure 2 depicts the MZI setup; Figure 7 illustrates the impact of losses on signal intensity and correlations; Figure 8 provides 2D maps of intensity and g(2) as a function of phase and mixing angle.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of quantifying quantum statistics in polaritonic circuits, presents a new theoretical framework (qPIC), analyzes single-waveguide MZI configurations, extends the model to integrated multi-mode circuits, and discusses the benefits of slow-light engineering and the impact of losses.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Strong light-matter coupling between a guided electromagnetic mode and an excitonic semiconductor transition gives rise to exciton-polaritons with optical nonlinearities far exceeding those of conventional photonic platforms. Utilizing these nonlinearities in the few-particle regime, where quantum signatures such as photon antibunching, sub-Poissonian statistics and non-trivial inter-mode correlations become accessible, is a central goal of integrated quantum photonics. Yet, a quantitative theoretical framework connecting realistic waveguide parameters to measurable non-classical photonic output is absent. Here, we present a comprehensive framework for predicting and benchmarking quantum photon statistics in polaritonic integrated circuits, using state-of-the-art experimentally achieved device parameters for (Al)GaAs waveguide platforms. By mapping the pulsed nonlinear waveguide dynamics onto a bosonic quantum circuit representation that explicitly incorporates dissipation, we identify experimentally accessible quantum signatures across two circuit configurations: a single waveguide in a free-space interferometric configuration and a fully integrated multimode coupled-waveguide circuit. We further show that slow-light engineering of the polariton dispersion offers a practical route to amplifying the effective nonlinearity, pushing quantum signatures beyond Gaussian statistics.

</details>

### [Inviscid scaling in the Kuramoto-Sivashinsky equation from functional renormalization group and direct numerical simulations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23364v1)

**Authors:** Liubov Gosteva, Dipankar Roy, Nicolás Wschebor, Léonie Canet  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.23364v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `non-equilibrium universality` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2605.23364_figures/2605.23364_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1. Evolution of the functions (a) ˆf ν κ and (b) ˆf D κ under the FRG flow, starting from the KS initial condition ˆf D Λ = 1, ˆf ν Λ = −1 + ˆp2 (black dashed lines) and reaching a fixed point when κ →0 (black solid lines correspond to κ/Λ = e−8). Inset of (b): Fixed point shape of ˆf ν κ(ˆω = 0, ˆp) (blue, dashed) and ˆf D κ (ˆω = 0, ˆp) (magenta, plain) recorded at κ/Λ = e−400. They are identical, which indicates that time-reversal symmetry emerges at large distances, and they identify with the KPZ fixed-point scaling function.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23364_figures/2605.23364_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2. Two-point correlation function C(t, p)/C(0, p) from DNS, plotted in logscales. The function C(t, p) is computed for times t = n/4 with n = 0, 1, 2, . . . from the simulations. The black line indicates the KPZ scaling z = 3/2, and the orange one the IB scaling z = 1. Inset: Extracted scaling functions, in the KPZ range (p from 0.02 to 0.1, circles), using the scaling variable x = pt2/3; in the IB range (p from 0.12 to 0.3, crosses), using the scaling variable x = pt. They are compared with the exact Prah¨ofer-Spohn scaling function for the KPZ fixed point (dash-dotted line), and with the exact asymptotic scaling function (7) from FRG for the IB fixed point (dashed line).</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2605.23364_figures/2605.23364_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 4. (a) Inverse of the decorrelation frequencies ϖα(p) from FRG; (b) decorrelation times τα(p) from DNS (see text for definition). Both show the IB scaling z = 1 over a range of intermediate momenta.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2605.23364_figures/2605.23364_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 3. Correlation function C(ω, p)/C(0, p) (a) from FRG; (b) from numerics. The KPZ and IB scaling regimes are in- dicated by the black and orange guidelines.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper identifies a new intermediate scaling regime in the Kuramoto-Sivashinsky equation characterized by an inviscid Burgers exponent of z=1. This regime emerges because the effective viscosity vanishes as the system flows from its microscopic unstable state to its macroscopic KPZ state. The findings are robustly supported by both functional renormalization group theory and large-scale numerical simulations.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The identification and characterization of a previously overlooked intermediate scaling regime in the one-dimensional Kuramoto-Sivashinsky (KS) equation.

**Main result.** The discovery of an 'Inviscid Burgers' scaling regime with a dynamical exponent z=1, which exists at intermediate scales between small-scale non-universal behavior and large-scale KPZ scaling (z=3/2).

**Method.** The study employs Functional Renormalization Group (FRG) using the Wetterich equation and Next-to-Leading-Order approximation, complemented by Direct Numerical Simulations (DNS) using a pseudo-spectral method.

**Model / system.** The one-dimensional Kuramoto-Sivashinsky (KS) equation, which describes systems with negative viscosity and positive fourth-order dissipation, relevant to chemical turbulence, flame fronts, and surface roughening.

**Key observables.** Dynamical exponent (z), effective viscosity (nu_kappa), two-point correlation function C(t, p), and time-reversal symmetry emergence.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Negative microscopic viscosity (nu < 0), positive fourth-order term (tau > 0), and the transition from the IB regime (z=1) to the KPZ regime (z=3/2).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The use of a Next-to-Leading-Order (NLO) approximation within the FRG framework and the introduction of a noise term to facilitate the study of scaling regimes.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the evolution of FRG functions and the convergence to a fixed point; Figure 2 shows DNS correlation function data collapse; Figure 3 compares the Fourier transform of the correlation function between FRG and DNS.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the KS equation and the problem of intermediate scaling, presents the FRG framework and results showing the vanishing effective viscosity, validates these findings with DNS, and concludes with the implications for universality classes.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We show that the one-dimensional Kuramoto-Sivashinsky (KS) equation features a scaling regime characterized by the dynamical exponent $z=1$ at intermediate scales between the large-scale Kardar-Parisi-Zhang (KPZ) scaling with $z=3/2$ and the small-scale non-universal behavior. This scaling regime is intrinsic to the KS dynamics since it arises from the vanishing of the effective viscosity when evolving from its microscopic negative KS value, to its macroscopic effective positive KPZ value. This vanishing of the viscosity deeply imprints the behavior of correlations at intermediate scales, which exhibit a universal $z=1$ scaling. This behavior pertains to the inviscid-Burgers universality class, which corresponds to the zero-viscosity fixed point of the KPZ equation. We evidence and characterize this so-far-overlooked scaling regime using both functional renormalization group and direct numerical simulations.

</details>

### [Quantum fluctuations in quartet superfluid of two-dimensional Fermi mixture](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.23267v1)

**Authors:** Wei Wang, Yupeng Wang, Xiaoling Cui

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2605.23267_figures/2605.23267_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2. Thermodynamic potential of QSF from quantum fluctuations (ΩQF) as a function of ln(˜µQ), with ˜µQ being the reduced chemical potential of quartet bosons (see defi- nition in Eq.(26)). The solid and dashed lines correspond to numerical results based on Eq.(25) and an analytical fit based on Eq.(27), respectively. **Summary.** This paper investigates quantum fluctuations in a 2D quartet superfluid made of one light and three heavy fermions. It demonstrates that including Gaussian fluctuations correctly recovers the expected bosonic equation of state in the deep binding limit. The work establishes a general framework for studying higher-order fermion correlations.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a theoretical framework for extending fluctuation theories from standard pairing to higher-order correlations, which is highly relevant for understanding many-body dynamics and complex cluster formation in ultracold gases.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study aims to understand quantum fluctuations in a quartet superfluid (QSF) of 2D mass-imbalanced Fermi mixtures and to determine if these clusters behave as composite bosons in the deep binding limit.

**Main result.** The theory successfully reproduces the logarithmic dependence of the 2D equation of state in the deep binding regime, confirming that quartet clusters behave as composite bosons.

**Method.** The authors use a functional path integral approach with an extended Gaussian fluctuation theory that incorporates dominant four-body correlations.

**Model / system.** A two-dimensional (2D) Fermi mixture with mass imbalance (heavy and light fermions) in a (1+3) cluster configuration, specifically considering realistic examples like 6Li-40K and 6Li-53Cr.

**Key observables.** Thermodynamic potential (Omega), equation of state (EoS), gap equation, number equations, and the quartet chemical potential.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Mass imbalance (mh, ml), 2D scattering length (a), quartet binding energy (E4), and the deep binding limit (reduced chemical potential approaching zero).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The study focuses on the zero-temperature (T=0) ground state and assumes a specific heavy-to-light number ratio of 3:1.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows diagrammatic representations of Green's functions and fluctuation matrix elements; Figure 2 plots the thermodynamic potential as a function of the logarithm of the reduced chemical potential for different mass-imbalanced systems.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of quartet superfluidity, presents a mean-field theory for (1+3) clusters, extends this to Gaussian fluctuation theory, provides analytical results for the deep binding limit, and validates the theory with numerical simulations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study quantum fluctuations in quartet superfluid (QSF) of two-dimensional (2D) fermion mixtures with mass imbalance. Here QSF is a high-order superfluid that corresponds to the condensation of ($1+3$) clusters, each consisting of a light fermion and three heavy ones. By incorporating the Gaussian fluctuations respecting dominant four-body correlations in this system, our theory successfully produces the logarithmic dependence of the 2D equation of state in the deep binding regime, thereby offering a correct physical picture of quartet clusters behaving as composite bosons. By extending the Gaussian fluctuation theory from pairing to quartet superfluids, our results shed light on quantum fluctuations in general fermion superfluids with arbitrarily high-order correlations.

</details>
